The 'Urfiyyah Has One Meaning: A Critical Refinement
Author refines the definition of 'urfiyyah and argues it has only one meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the 'urfiyyah proposition has only one meaning, unlike the conditional (mashrūṭah), and identify when a description has 'entry into permanence'.

Core Idea
Permanence, unlike necessity, does not split the 'urfiyyah into two meanings.

In this passage, the commentator refines the definition of the 'urfiyyah (habitual) proposition by arguing against those who think it has two meanings analogous to the conditional. He demonstrates that permanence (dawām) behaves differently from necessity (ḍarūrah): if the predicate is permanently true of the composite of essence and description, it is also permanently true of the essence alone at the time of that description. Hence, the 'urfiyyah has a single meaning: the judgment of permanent affirmation of the predicate to the composite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term 'urfiyyah and note how the author defines it: permanent affirmation to the composite of essence and description.
2
Compare with the conditional (mashrūṭah)
Understand why the conditional has two meanings. For necessity, judging that the predicate is necessary for the composite differs from judging it necessary for the essence at the time of the description. For permanence, these coincide.
3
Examine the example
Look at the example 'Every writer is moving of fingers'. The predicate holds as long as the subject is a writer, regardless of whether the predicate is permanently true of the person.
4
Check the author's conclusion
The author insists that the 'urfiyyah has one meaning only, and the description does not have 'entry into permanence' in the same way as in the conditional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا قلنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع مثلاً وهو فى معنى كل شخص كاتب متحرك الاصابع كان المعنى اثبات تحرك الاصابع للكاتب لا الشخص، نعم فرق بين الايجاب والنفي من حيث ان النفي يفيد ثبوت اصل الحكم والاثبات لا يفيد نفى اصل الحكم وهذا القدر لا يوجب اختصاص فهم العرف هذا المعنى بالسالبة دون الموجبة فتقطن. ثم يظهر من بعض المحققين ان فهم هذا المعنى انما هو فيا اذا كان للوصف مدخل في الدوام كقولنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع ولاشيء من الكاتب بساكن الاصابع واما اذا لم يكن له مدخل فيه فلا ، كقولنا كل كاتب حيوان ولاشيء من وقد ظهر لك مما تلوناه ان كون الوصف دخيلاً في الدوام ليس له مدخل في فهم العرف هذا المعنى، بل كما يفهم هذا المعنى من نحو كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع فكذا يفهم من نحو: «كل كاتب الكاتب بحجر. ثابتة له مطلقا فهو شي حيوان ان الحيوانية ثابتة للموضوع مادام كاتباً وما يترأى فى الخارج من انها ثابر آخر وكلامنا في دلالة اللفظ من حيث هو هو من غير نظر إلى النسبة الخارجية فتأمل. (ميرزا محمد علی) (۸۴) اى عند عدم ذكر الجهة فى القضية الموجبة والسالبة، لا في الموجبة فقط كما هو المتبادر من كلامه : لوم اسلامی ثم اعلم انهم لم يعتبروا للعرفية معنيين على قياس معنى المشروطة اذ الحال بالنسبة الى الضرورة يتفاوت بين الحكم بثبوت المحمول المجموع الذات والوصف العنواني و بين الحكم بثبوته للذات في زمان ذلك الوصف على مالوحنا اليه بخلاف الحال بالنسبة الى الدوام فانه لا تفاوت بين الحكمين فيه اذ كل مادة صدق فيها الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات والوصف يصدق فيها الحكم بدوامه في زمان ذلك الوصف فلم يحصل للعرفية معنيان بل لها معنى واحد اعنى الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات و الوصف ففى العرفية لا يتيسر ان يكون للوصف مدخل فى دوام ثبوت المحمول بالمعنى المذكور في المشروطة لان الدوام كما يتحقق بالنسبة الى مجموع الذات والوصف يتحقق بالنسبة الى الذات وحده في زمان ذلك الوصف فلا يصح ان يقال: لولم يعتبر الوصف مع الذات مركباً لم يتحقق الدوام. (عبد الرحيم ) (۸۵) تفریح لفهم هذا المعنى من القضية مطلقا لكن اتى بالموجبة، لانها موضع الشبهة و محل الريبة لا لفهمه من الموجبة بخصوصها على ما هو المتبادر فانه لا يناسب قوله: «عند الاطلاق» على ما ذكرنا كما هو ظاهر لمن له دربة بسياق الكلام. اللهم الا ان يقال ان قوله عند الاطلاق قيد للموجبة وحدها و حذف هذا القيد من السالبة بقرينته فحينئذ يجوز ان يكون ذلك تفريعاً للموجبة بخصوصها ايضاً لكن حقيقة الأمر ظاهرة لارباب الحقيقة. (ميرزا محمد علی) (۸۶) فانها هي العرفية العامة المقيدة باللادوام الذاتي و ظاهر ان المطلق عام من المقيد. (میرزا محمد علی) (۸۷) قوله: «في احد الازمنة الثلاثة»: لا يحق أنه ليس ذلك تفسيراً لقوله : بالفعل، كما يظهر من بعض المحققين من المحشين بل هو متعلق بقوله : متحققة بالفعل، ومعنى الفعلية: الخروج من القوة الى الفعل. و تحقيق ذلك انه لمافسر المطلقة العامة بالقضية التي حكم فيها بكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل وكان بظاهره يوهم ان تحققها الفعلى انما هو فى الأن الحاضر، قيده بقوله: «فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة اشارة الى ان المطلقة العامة ما حكم فيها بتحقق النسبة بالفعل في احد الازمنة لا فى زمان الحال كما هو المتبادر من ظاهره فح نقول : ان قوله : «اى : فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة» اما تفسير لمحذوف متعلق بقوله: «متحققة بالفعل فيكون تقدير الكلام انها ما حكم فيها يكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل في زمان اى فى احد الازمنة و يكون فايدة التفسير ان ليس المراد منه زمان الحاضر على التعيين كما هو الظاهر، او لمفعول مطلق محذوف اى متحققة بالفعل تحققاً اى تحققاً كائناً فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة ولا يخفى فايدة التفسير على هذا التقدير ايضاً. فان قيل : فعلى ما ذكر من معنى المطلقة العامة يلزم ان لا تكون القضية التي موضوعها وقت مطلقة عامة كقولنا الزمان موجود مثلاً والالزم ان يكون للزمان زمان. قلنا لاضرر ، فان الزمان الذى هو ظرف زمان اعتبارى لا حقيق والممتنع ان يكون كلاهما حقيقياً لامطلقا. لهاء بقى هنا شيء و هو ما قيل: من ان الفعلية ـة كما صرح به شارح المطالع ويدل عليه تفسير هم كـ ليست بجهة القضية فان الجهة كما تقدم هى الكيفية الحاصلة لوقوع النسبة الذى هو الحكم ولاشك في كونها مغايرة للنسبة فان الجهة جزء اخير للقضية مغاير للموضوع و المحمول والحكم والفعلية المفسرة بما ذكر هو معنى الحكم والوقوع لا غير، فح لا يصح ذكر المطلقة العامة في الموجهات وجعلها ثمانية كما فعله المصنف وغيره. و اجاب ذلك المحقق و تبعه بعض المحققين بعد تسليمه ان الفعلية ليست بجهة بان عد المطلقة عله هم العامة في عداد الموجهات كعدهم السوالب فى الحمليات يشير الى أن المطلقة العامة لما كانت مستعدة القبول الجهات وصالحة لدخولها عليها عدوها منها كما عدوا السوالب من الحمليات لذلك. و اقول: هذا كما قيل - ينافى ماسيأتى من ان الدائمة المطلقة تناقض المطلقة العامة مع اشتراطهم في التناقض الاختلاف في الجهة، ولو سلم عدم المنافات بناء على ما سيأتى فالاولى ان يقال بان الفعلية جهة كما صرح به المصنف في شرح الرسالة وذلك لان القضية قبل تقييدها بالفعلية تحتمل الفعلية و غيرها فاذا قيدت بها اختصت بها. والحاصل : ان الفعلية لا تكون جهة اذا دلت على ان النسبة ليست بمقيدة بشيء من الفعلية وغيرها لا اذا دلت على كونها مقيدة بالفعلية و الاطلاق فافهم (میرزا محمد علی) ( وقال الشيخ عبد الرحيم في تحقيق المقام) : ... ثم اعلم ان المصنف ذهب الى ان الفعلية كيفية ). النسبة لأن معناها ليس الاوقوع النسبة و .... هذا كلام حق لكن يفهم من قوله: كما عدوا السالبة الخ ان اطلاق الحملية والشرطية على السوالب بالمجاز و هو خلاف ما مر فتذكر». (۸۸) يريد ان هذا المعنى اعنى الحكم يكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل في أحد الازمنة الثلاثة لما
So if we say: 'Every writer is moving of fingers' for example, and it is in the meaning of 'Every person who is a writer is moving of fingers', then the meaning is affirmation of moving of fingers to the writer, not to the person. Yes, there is a difference between affirmation and negation in that negation establishes the root of the judgment while affirmation does not entail negation of the root of the judgment. And this amount does not necessitate that the common understanding of this meaning is specific to the negative proposition without the affirmative, so be attentive. Then it appears from some investigators that understanding this meaning is only when the description has an entry into permanence, like our saying: 'Every writer is moving of fingers' and 'No writer is still of fingers'. But when it has no entry into it, then not, like our saying: 'Every writer is an animal' and 'No writer is a stone'. And it has become apparent to you from what we have recited that the fact that the description is an entry into permanence has no entry into the common understanding of this meaning; rather, just as this meaning is understood from something like 'Every writer is moving of fingers', so too it is understood from something like: 'Every writer is an animal' that animality is established for the subject as long as he is a writer. And what appears externally that it is permanently established for it is another matter, and our speech is concerning the indication of the word in itself without consideration of the external relation, so reflect. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (84) i.e., when the modality is not mentioned in the affirmative and negative proposition, not only in the affirmative as is apparent from his statement: ... Then know that they did not consider for the 'urfiyyah two meanings on the analogy of the meaning of the conditional (mashrūṭah), because the situation with respect to necessity differs between the judgment of affirming the predicate to the composite of essence and the attributive description and the judgment of affirming it to the essence in the time of that description, as we indicated. But the situation with respect to permanence is different: there is no difference between the two judgments in it, because every matter in which the judgment of the permanence of the affirmation of the predicate to the composite of essence and description is true, the judgment of its permanence in the time of that description is also true. So the 'urfiyyah did not acquire two meanings; rather it has one meaning, namely the judgment of the permanence of the affirmation of the predicate to the composite of essence and description. Thus in the 'urfiyyah it is not possible for the description to have an entry into the permanence of the affirmation of the predicate in the sense mentioned in the conditional, because permanence, just as it is realized with respect to the composite of essence and description, is also realized with respect to the essence alone in the time of that description. So it cannot be said: 'If the description were not considered with the essence as a composite, permanence would not be realized.' (Abd al-Rahim) (85) A branching for understanding this meaning from the proposition absolutely, but he brought the affirmative because it is the place of doubt and the locus of suspicion, not for understanding it from the affirmative specifically, as might be apparent, for it does not suit his statement 'when unrestricted' according to what we have mentioned, as is clear to one who has practice with the flow of speech. Unless it be said that his statement 'when unrestricted' is a restriction for the affirmative alone, and this restriction is omitted from the negative by its context, then it is possible that this branching is for the affirmative specifically as well, but the reality of the matter is apparent to the people of reality. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (86) For it is the general 'urfiyyah restricted by non-permanent essence, and it is apparent that the absolute is more general than the restricted. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (87) His statement: 'in one of the three times': it is not correct that this is an interpretation of his statement 'by actuality', as appears from some investigators among the glossators; rather it is attached to his statement 'actually realized', and the meaning of actuality is the exit from potentiality to act. And the verification of that is that when the general absolute was interpreted as the proposition in which judgment is made that the relation is actually realized, and its apparent meaning would suggest that its actual realization is only in the present moment, he restricted it with his statement 'in one of the three times' as an indication that the general absolute is that in which judgment is made of the actual realization of the relation in one of the three times, not in the time of the present as is apparent from its surface. So we say: His statement 'i.e., in one of the three times' is either an interpretation of a deleted phrase attached to his statement 'actually realized', so the estimation of the speech would be: it is that in which judgment is made that the relation is actually realized in a time, i.e., in one of the three times, and the benefit of the interpretation is that what is intended is not specifically the present time as is apparent; or it is for a deleted verbal noun, i.e., actually realized with a realization, i.e., a realization occurring in one of the three times, and the benefit of the interpretation is not hidden on this assumption either. For if it is said: According to what is mentioned of the meaning of the general absolute, it would entail that a proposition whose subject is time would not be a general absolute, like our saying 'Time exists', for example, and the entailment would be that time has a time. We say: No harm, for time which is a container is a conceptual time, not real, and the impossible is that both be real, not absolute. Some things remain: It is said that actuality—as stated by the commentator of al-Matali' and indicated by their interpretation—is not a modality of the proposition. For modality, as was mentioned, is the quality resulting from the occurrence of the relation, which is the judgment, and there is no doubt that it is distinct from the relation, for modality is a final part of the proposition distinct from the subject, predicate, and judgment. And actuality interpreted as mentioned is the meaning of the judgment and occurrence, nothing else. So it is not correct to include the general absolute among the modal propositions and make them eight as the author and others did. And that investigator responded—and some investigators followed him—after conceding that actuality is not a modality, by saying that their counting of the general absolute among the modal propositions is like their counting of negatives among the categoricals, indicating that the general absolute, since it is receptive to modalities and suitable for them to enter upon it, they counted it among them, just as they counted negatives among the categoricals for that reason. And I say: This, as has been said, contradicts what will come: that the permanent absolute contradicts the general absolute, while they require in contradiction difference in modality. Even if the lack of contradiction is conceded based on what will come, it is more appropriate to say that actuality is a modality, as the author stated in Sharh al-Risalah, because the proposition before it is restricted by actuality is possible for actuality and other than it, so when it is restricted by it, it becomes specific to it. The result: actuality is not a modality if it indicates that the relation is not restricted by anything of actuality and other than it; but if it indicates that it is restricted by actuality and unqualifiedness, then it is. So understand. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (And Shaykh Abd al-Rahim said in the verification of the topic): ... Then know that the author held that actuality is a quality of the relation because its meaning is nothing but the occurrence of the relation... This speech is true, but it is understood from his statement 'as they counted the negative' that the application of 'categorical' and 'conditional' to negatives is metaphorical, and this contradicts what has passed, so remember. (88) He intends that this meaning—i.e., the judgment that the relation is actually realized in one of the three times—for what?
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a critical super-commentary (hashiya) from Yazdi’s gloss on earlier logical works. It first addresses the 'urfiyyah (habitual) proposition, then moves to the mutlaqah 'āmmah (general absolute) and the debate on whether actuality (fi'liyyah) counts as a modality (jihah).

The opening statement discusses an example: 'Every writer is moving of fingers.' The author clarifies that the predicate 'moving of fingers' is affirmed of the writer qua writer, not of the person in general. This meaning is understood regardless of whether the description (being a writer) is essential to the permanence of the judgment. The author insists that common understanding does not distinguish between affirmative and negative in this regard.

Then, the author notes that some scholars think the description only enters into permanence in cases like 'every writer is moving of fingers' (where the predicate is not permanent for the person as such), but not in cases like 'every writer is an animal' (where the predicate is always true of the person). However, the author corrects this: the meaning is the same—the predicate is affirmed as long as the subject has the description. The difference lies in external reality, not in the linguistic indication.

Regarding the 'urfiyyah itself, the author states that it does not have two meanings like the conditional (mashrūṭah). In the conditional, there is a difference between judging that the predicate is necessary for the composite (essence+description) and judging that it is necessary for the essence alone at the time of the description. But for permanence, these two judgments coincide: if the predicate is permanently true of the composite, it is also permanently true of the essence at the time of the description. Hence, the 'urfiyyah has one meaning: the judgment of permanent affirmation of the predicate to the composite of essence and description. The description cannot be said to 'enter into' permanence in a way that makes it essential, because permanence is preserved either way.

Then the discussion shifts to the mutlaqah 'āmmah (general absolute). The definition given: a proposition in which it is judged that the relation is actually realized (bi al-fi'l). There is a nuance: 'actually realized' might be misunderstood as only in the present moment. So it is qualified by 'in one of the three times' (past, present, future). The author explains two ways to parse this qualification: either as an interpretation of an omitted phrase or as a verbal noun indicating the kind of actualization.

A potential objection is raised: if time itself is the subject, e.g., 'Time exists', then the proposition would have a subject that is time, and time cannot be in time—so would such a proposition not be general absolute? The answer: time as a container is conceptual, not real, so no actual temporal container is needed.

Finally, a major debate: is actuality (fi'liyyah) a modality? Some scholars, including the commentator of al-Matali', say no: because a modality must be a quality distinct from the relation itself. Actuality, as 'the occurrence of the relation', is just the judgment, not a separate modality. Therefore, they argue, the general absolute should not be counted among the modal propositions (which number eight in the standard list). The response given (attributed to a muhaqqiq and followed by others) is that the general absolute is counted among modals because it is receptive to modalities; similarly, negative propositions are counted among categoricals even though negation is not a modality. The author of the gloss (Yazdi) criticizes this response, pointing out that it contradicts the later rule that the permanent absolute contradicts the general absolute, which requires difference in modality. Instead, Yazdi prefers the view of the author of the original work (al-Sullam or Sharh al-Risalah) that actuality is indeed a modality, because before restriction the proposition could be actual or possible, and restriction narrows it to actuality.

The passage concludes with a subtle distinction: actuality is not a modality if it means the relation is unrestricted (i.e., just 'occurs' without specifying actuality), but it is a modality if it means the relation is restricted to actual existence. This reflects the idea that 'actuality' as a modality is a qualification, not merely the fact of occurrence.

All examples in this commentary are drawn from the text itself, which uses logical examples from the Islamic tradition (e.g., 'writer', 'animal', 'moving of fingers'). No secular examples are introduced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the 'urfiyyah have only one meaning according to the text?
A) Because permanence, unlike necessity, does not differentiate between the composite and the time-bound judgment.
B) Because the 'urfiyyah only appears in negative propositions.
C) Because the description in the 'urfiyyah is always essential.
D) Because the conditional is not a modal proposition.

Key Takeaway
The 'urfiyyah proposition has a single meaning due to the nature of permanence, unlike the conditional's two meanings due to necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyse the proposition: 'Every slave who is freed is entitled to marry.' Is this an 'urfiyyah? Identify the composite of essence and description, and explain whether the predicate is permanent for that composite. Does the description (being freed) have an 'entry into permanence'?
?
Compare: 'Every freed slave is a human' and 'Every freed slave is indebted.' Which one is an 'urfiyyah? Justify using the definition from this lesson.

Propositions
intermediate
10 min
The General Absolute: Actuality Realized in One of Three Times
Author refines the definition of mutlaqah 'āmmah by clarifying the temporal scope of actuality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the general absolute proposition and explain why the qualification 'in one of the three times' resolves an apparent ambiguity about actuality.

Core Idea
Actuality is not the present moment; it spans past, present, and future.

The commentator clarifies the definition of the general absolute (al-muṭlaqah al-‘āmmah) by addressing a potential misunderstanding: 'actually realized' might be taken to mean only in the present. He explains that actuality (al-fi‘liyyah) means the relation is realized in any of the three times, not necessarily the present. This qualification preserves the generality of the proposition and prevents confusion when the subject is time itself.

Guided Path
1
Find the definition of mutlaqah 'āmmah
Locate the phrase 'the proposition in which judgment is made that the relation is actually realized'.
This is the base definition.
2
Identify the ambiguity
Why might someone think actuality means only the present? The word 'actual' often suggests current reality. The comment 'in one of the three times' is added to clarify.
3
See how it is resolved
The comment 'i.e., in one of the three times' is attached to 'actually realized' to indicate that any time suffices.
The author gives two possible grammatical explanations for this attachment.
4
Consider the objection of time as subject
If the subject is time itself (e.g., 'Time exists'), does that violate the definition? The answer distinguishes conceptual time from real time.
Only real time is problematic, but time as a container is conceptual, so no issue.

فاذا قلنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع مثلاً وهو فى معنى كل شخص كاتب متحرك الاصابع كان المعنى اثبات تحرك الاصابع للكاتب لا الشخص، نعم فرق بين الايجاب والنفي من حيث ان النفي يفيد ثبوت اصل الحكم والاثبات لا يفيد نفى اصل الحكم وهذا القدر لا يوجب اختصاص فهم العرف هذا المعنى بالسالبة دون الموجبة فتقطن. ثم يظهر من بعض المحققين ان فهم هذا المعنى انما هو فيا اذا كان للوصف مدخل في الدوام كقولنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع ولاشيء من الكاتب بساكن الاصابع واما اذا لم يكن له مدخل فيه فلا ، كقولنا كل كاتب حيوان ولاشيء من وقد ظهر لك مما تلوناه ان كون الوصف دخيلاً في الدوام ليس له مدخل في فهم العرف هذا المعنى، بل كما يفهم هذا المعنى من نحو كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع فكذا يفهم من نحو: «كل كاتب الكاتب بحجر. ثابتة له مطلقا فهو شي حيوان ان الحيوانية ثابتة للموضوع مادام كاتباً وما يترأى فى الخارج من انها ثابر آخر وكلامنا في دلالة اللفظ من حيث هو هو من غير نظر إلى النسبة الخارجية فتأمل. (ميرزا محمد علی) (۸۴) اى عند عدم ذكر الجهة فى القضية الموجبة والسالبة، لا في الموجبة فقط كما هو المتبادر من كلامه : لوم اسلامی ثم اعلم انهم لم يعتبروا للعرفية معنيين على قياس معنى المشروطة اذ الحال بالنسبة الى الضرورة يتفاوت بين الحكم بثبوت المحمول المجموع الذات والوصف العنواني و بين الحكم بثبوته للذات في زمان ذلك الوصف على مالوحنا اليه بخلاف الحال بالنسبة الى الدوام فانه لا تفاوت بين الحكمين فيه اذ كل مادة صدق فيها الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات والوصف يصدق فيها الحكم بدوامه في زمان ذلك الوصف فلم يحصل للعرفية معنيان بل لها معنى واحد اعنى الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات و الوصف ففى العرفية لا يتيسر ان يكون للوصف مدخل فى دوام ثبوت المحمول بالمعنى المذكور في المشروطة لان الدوام كما يتحقق بالنسبة الى مجموع الذات والوصف يتحقق بالنسبة الى الذات وحده في زمان ذلك الوصف فلا يصح ان يقال: لولم يعتبر الوصف مع الذات مركباً لم يتحقق الدوام. (عبد الرحيم ) (۸۵) تفریح لفهم هذا المعنى من القضية مطلقا لكن اتى بالموجبة، لانها موضع الشبهة و محل الريبة لا لفهمه من الموجبة بخصوصها على ما هو المتبادر فانه لا يناسب قوله: «عند الاطلاق» على ما ذكرنا كما هو ظاهر لمن له دربة بسياق الكلام. اللهم الا ان يقال ان قوله عند الاطلاق قيد للموجبة وحدها و حذف هذا القيد من السالبة بقرينته فحينئذ يجوز ان يكون ذلك تفريعاً للموجبة بخصوصها ايضاً لكن حقيقة الأمر ظاهرة لارباب الحقيقة. (ميرزا محمد علی) (۸۶) فانها هي العرفية العامة المقيدة باللادوام الذاتي و ظاهر ان المطلق عام من المقيد. (میرزا محمد علی) (۸۷) قوله: «في احد الازمنة الثلاثة»: لا يحق أنه ليس ذلك تفسيراً لقوله : بالفعل، كما يظهر من بعض المحققين من المحشين بل هو متعلق بقوله : متحققة بالفعل، ومعنى الفعلية: الخروج من القوة الى الفعل. و تحقيق ذلك انه لمافسر المطلقة العامة بالقضية التي حكم فيها بكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل وكان بظاهره يوهم ان تحققها الفعلى انما هو فى الأن الحاضر، قيده بقوله: «فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة اشارة الى ان المطلقة العامة ما حكم فيها بتحقق النسبة بالفعل في احد الازمنة لا فى زمان الحال كما هو المتبادر من ظاهره فح نقول : ان قوله : «اى : فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة» اما تفسير لمحذوف متعلق بقوله: «متحققة بالفعل فيكون تقدير الكلام انها ما حكم فيها يكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل في زمان اى فى احد الازمنة و يكون فايدة التفسير ان ليس المراد منه زمان الحاضر على التعيين كما هو الظاهر، او لمفعول مطلق محذوف اى متحققة بالفعل تحققاً اى تحققاً كائناً فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة ولا يخفى فايدة التفسير على هذا التقدير ايضاً. فان قيل : فعلى ما ذكر من معنى المطلقة العامة يلزم ان لا تكون القضية التي موضوعها وقت مطلقة عامة كقولنا الزمان موجود مثلاً والالزم ان يكون للزمان زمان. قلنا لاضرر ، فان الزمان الذى هو ظرف زمان اعتبارى لا حقيق والممتنع ان يكون كلاهما حقيقياً لامطلقا. لهاء بقى هنا شيء و هو ما قيل: من ان الفعلية ـة كما صرح به شارح المطالع ويدل عليه تفسير هم كـ ليست بجهة القضية فان الجهة كما تقدم هى الكيفية الحاصلة لوقوع النسبة الذى هو الحكم ولاشك في كونها مغايرة للنسبة فان الجهة جزء اخير للقضية مغاير للموضوع و المحمول والحكم والفعلية المفسرة بما ذكر هو معنى الحكم والوقوع لا غير، فح لا يصح ذكر المطلقة العامة في الموجهات وجعلها ثمانية كما فعله المصنف وغيره. و اجاب ذلك المحقق و تبعه بعض المحققين بعد تسليمه ان الفعلية ليست بجهة بان عد المطلقة عله هم العامة في عداد الموجهات كعدهم السوالب فى الحمليات يشير الى أن المطلقة العامة لما كانت مستعدة القبول الجهات وصالحة لدخولها عليها عدوها منها كما عدوا السوالب من الحمليات لذلك. و اقول: هذا كما قيل - ينافى ماسيأتى من ان الدائمة المطلقة تناقض المطلقة العامة مع اشتراطهم في التناقض الاختلاف في الجهة، ولو سلم عدم المنافات بناء على ما سيأتى فالاولى ان يقال بان الفعلية جهة كما صرح به المصنف في شرح الرسالة وذلك لان القضية قبل تقييدها بالفعلية تحتمل الفعلية و غيرها فاذا قيدت بها اختصت بها. والحاصل : ان الفعلية لا تكون جهة اذا دلت على ان النسبة ليست بمقيدة بشيء من الفعلية وغيرها لا اذا دلت على كونها مقيدة بالفعلية و الاطلاق فافهم (میرزا محمد علی) ( وقال الشيخ عبد الرحيم في تحقيق المقام) : ... ثم اعلم ان المصنف ذهب الى ان الفعلية كيفية ). النسبة لأن معناها ليس الاوقوع النسبة و .... هذا كلام حق لكن يفهم من قوله: كما عدوا السالبة الخ ان اطلاق الحملية والشرطية على السوالب بالمجاز و هو خلاف ما مر فتذكر». (۸۸) يريد ان هذا المعنى اعنى الحكم يكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل في أحد الازمنة الثلاثة لما
So if we say: 'Every writer is moving of fingers' for example, and it is in the meaning of 'Every person who is a writer is moving of fingers', then the meaning is affirmation of moving of fingers to the writer, not to the person. Yes, there is a difference between affirmation and negation in that negation establishes the root of the judgment while affirmation does not entail negation of the root of the judgment. And this amount does not necessitate that the common understanding of this meaning is specific to the negative proposition without the affirmative, so be attentive. Then it appears from some investigators that understanding this meaning is only when the description has an entry into permanence, like our saying: 'Every writer is moving of fingers' and 'No writer is still of fingers'. But when it has no entry into it, then not, like our saying: 'Every writer is an animal' and 'No writer is a stone'. And it has become apparent to you from what we have recited that the fact that the description is an entry into permanence has no entry into the common understanding of this meaning; rather, just as this meaning is understood from something like 'Every writer is moving of fingers', so too it is understood from something like: 'Every writer is an animal' that animality is established for the subject as long as he is a writer. And what appears externally that it is permanently established for it is another matter, and our speech is concerning the indication of the word in itself without consideration of the external relation, so reflect. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (84) i.e., when the modality is not mentioned in the affirmative and negative proposition, not only in the affirmative as is apparent from his statement: ... Then know that they did not consider for the 'urfiyyah two meanings on the analogy of the meaning of the conditional (mashrūṭah), because the situation with respect to necessity differs between the judgment of affirming the predicate to the composite of essence and the attributive description and the judgment of affirming it to the essence in the time of that description, as we indicated. But the situation with respect to permanence is different: there is no difference between the two judgments in it, because every matter in which the judgment of the permanence of the affirmation of the predicate to the composite of essence and description is true, the judgment of its permanence in the time of that description is also true. So the 'urfiyyah did not acquire two meanings; rather it has one meaning, namely the judgment of the permanence of the affirmation of the predicate to the composite of essence and description. Thus in the 'urfiyyah it is not possible for the description to have an entry into the permanence of the affirmation of the predicate in the sense mentioned in the conditional, because permanence, just as it is realized with respect to the composite of essence and description, is also realized with respect to the essence alone in the time of that description. So it cannot be said: 'If the description were not considered with the essence as a composite, permanence would not be realized.' (Abd al-Rahim) (85) A branching for understanding this meaning from the proposition absolutely, but he brought the affirmative because it is the place of doubt and the locus of suspicion, not for understanding it from the affirmative specifically, as might be apparent, for it does not suit his statement 'when unrestricted' according to what we have mentioned, as is clear to one who has practice with the flow of speech. Unless it be said that his statement 'when unrestricted' is a restriction for the affirmative alone, and this restriction is omitted from the negative by its context, then it is possible that this branching is for the affirmative specifically as well, but the reality of the matter is apparent to the people of reality. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (86) For it is the general 'urfiyyah restricted by non-permanent essence, and it is apparent that the absolute is more general than the restricted. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (87) His statement: 'in one of the three times': it is not correct that this is an interpretation of his statement 'by actuality', as appears from some investigators among the glossators; rather it is attached to his statement 'actually realized', and the meaning of actuality is the exit from potentiality to act. And the verification of that is that when the general absolute was interpreted as the proposition in which judgment is made that the relation is actually realized, and its apparent meaning would suggest that its actual realization is only in the present moment, he restricted it with his statement 'in one of the three times' as an indication that the general absolute is that in which judgment is made of the actual realization of the relation in one of the three times, not in the time of the present as is apparent from its surface. So we say: His statement 'i.e., in one of the three times' is either an interpretation of a deleted phrase attached to his statement 'actually realized', so the estimation of the speech would be: it is that in which judgment is made that the relation is actually realized in a time, i.e., in one of the three times, and the benefit of the interpretation is that what is intended is not specifically the present time as is apparent; or it is for a deleted verbal noun, i.e., actually realized with a realization, i.e., a realization occurring in one of the three times, and the benefit of the interpretation is not hidden on this assumption either. For if it is said: According to what is mentioned of the meaning of the general absolute, it would entail that a proposition whose subject is time would not be a general absolute, like our saying 'Time exists', for example, and the entailment would be that time has a time. We say: No harm, for time which is a container is a conceptual time, not real, and the impossible is that both be real, not absolute. Some things remain: It is said that actuality—as stated by the commentator of al-Matali' and indicated by their interpretation—is not a modality of the proposition. For modality, as was mentioned, is the quality resulting from the occurrence of the relation, which is the judgment, and there is no doubt that it is distinct from the relation, for modality is a final part of the proposition distinct from the subject, predicate, and judgment. And actuality interpreted as mentioned is the meaning of the judgment and occurrence, nothing else. So it is not correct to include the general absolute among the modal propositions and make them eight as the author and others did. And that investigator responded—and some investigators followed him—after conceding that actuality is not a modality, by saying that their counting of the general absolute among the modal propositions is like their counting of negatives among the categoricals, indicating that the general absolute, since it is receptive to modalities and suitable for them to enter upon it, they counted it among them, just as they counted negatives among the categoricals for that reason. And I say: This, as has been said, contradicts what will come: that the permanent absolute contradicts the general absolute, while they require in contradiction difference in modality. Even if the lack of contradiction is conceded based on what will come, it is more appropriate to say that actuality is a modality, as the author stated in Sharh al-Risalah, because the proposition before it is restricted by actuality is possible for actuality and other than it, so when it is restricted by it, it becomes specific to it. The result: actuality is not a modality if it indicates that the relation is not restricted by anything of actuality and other than it; but if it indicates that it is restricted by actuality and unqualifiedness, then it is. So understand. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (And Shaykh Abd al-Rahim said in the verification of the topic): ... Then know that the author held that actuality is a quality of the relation because its meaning is nothing but the occurrence of the relation... This speech is true, but it is understood from his statement 'as they counted the negative' that the application of 'categorical' and 'conditional' to negatives is metaphorical, and this contradicts what has passed, so remember. (88) He intends that this meaning—i.e., the judgment that the relation is actually realized in one of the three times—for what?
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a critical super-commentary (hashiya) from Yazdi’s gloss on earlier logical works. It first addresses the 'urfiyyah (habitual) proposition, then moves to the mutlaqah 'āmmah (general absolute) and the debate on whether actuality (fi'liyyah) counts as a modality (jihah).

The opening statement discusses an example: 'Every writer is moving of fingers.' The author clarifies that the predicate 'moving of fingers' is affirmed of the writer qua writer, not of the person in general. This meaning is understood regardless of whether the description (being a writer) is essential to the permanence of the judgment. The author insists that common understanding does not distinguish between affirmative and negative in this regard.

Then, the author notes that some scholars think the description only enters into permanence in cases like 'every writer is moving of fingers' (where the predicate is not permanent for the person as such), but not in cases like 'every writer is an animal' (where the predicate is always true of the person). However, the author corrects this: the meaning is the same—the predicate is affirmed as long as the subject has the description. The difference lies in external reality, not in the linguistic indication.

Regarding the 'urfiyyah itself, the author states that it does not have two meanings like the conditional (mashrūṭah). In the conditional, there is a difference between judging that the predicate is necessary for the composite (essence+description) and judging that it is necessary for the essence alone at the time of the description. But for permanence, these two judgments coincide: if the predicate is permanently true of the composite, it is also permanently true of the essence at the time of the description. Hence, the 'urfiyyah has one meaning: the judgment of permanent affirmation of the predicate to the composite of essence and description. The description cannot be said to 'enter into' permanence in a way that makes it essential, because permanence is preserved either way.

Then the discussion shifts to the mutlaqah 'āmmah (general absolute). The definition given: a proposition in which it is judged that the relation is actually realized (bi al-fi'l). There is a nuance: 'actually realized' might be misunderstood as only in the present moment. So it is qualified by 'in one of the three times' (past, present, future). The author explains two ways to parse this qualification: either as an interpretation of an omitted phrase or as a verbal noun indicating the kind of actualization.

A potential objection is raised: if time itself is the subject, e.g., 'Time exists', then the proposition would have a subject that is time, and time cannot be in time—so would such a proposition not be general absolute? The answer: time as a container is conceptual, not real, so no actual temporal container is needed.

Finally, a major debate: is actuality (fi'liyyah) a modality? Some scholars, including the commentator of al-Matali', say no: because a modality must be a quality distinct from the relation itself. Actuality, as 'the occurrence of the relation', is just the judgment, not a separate modality. Therefore, they argue, the general absolute should not be counted among the modal propositions (which number eight in the standard list). The response given (attributed to a muhaqqiq and followed by others) is that the general absolute is counted among modals because it is receptive to modalities; similarly, negative propositions are counted among categoricals even though negation is not a modality. The author of the gloss (Yazdi) criticizes this response, pointing out that it contradicts the later rule that the permanent absolute contradicts the general absolute, which requires difference in modality. Instead, Yazdi prefers the view of the author of the original work (al-Sullam or Sharh al-Risalah) that actuality is indeed a modality, because before restriction the proposition could be actual or possible, and restriction narrows it to actuality.

The passage concludes with a subtle distinction: actuality is not a modality if it means the relation is unrestricted (i.e., just 'occurs' without specifying actuality), but it is a modality if it means the relation is restricted to actual existence. This reflects the idea that 'actuality' as a modality is a qualification, not merely the fact of occurrence.

All examples in this commentary are drawn from the text itself, which uses logical examples from the Islamic tradition (e.g., 'writer', 'animal', 'moving of fingers'). No secular examples are introduced.

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of adding 'in one of the three times' to the definition of the general absolute?
A) To restrict actuality to the past only.
B) To indicate that actuality is not limited to the present moment.
C) To exclude future events from being general absolute.
D) To change the definition entirely.

Key Takeaway
The general absolute is defined by actual realization in any of the three times, not just the present.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify the following proposition as a general absolute or not: 'The resurrection will happen in the future.' Explain your reasoning using the definition from this lesson. Does it satisfy the condition of actuality in one of the three times?
?
Consider the proposition: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) was born in Mecca.' Is this a general absolute? Why or why not? Identify the time involved.

Is Actuality a Modality? A Critical Examination
Author debates whether actuality is a modality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the debate on whether actuality (fi'liyyah) is a genuine modality and evaluate the two main positions.

Core Idea
Actuality is a modality if it restricts the relation, not if it merely indicates occurrence.

A major dispute in modal logic is whether the actuality expressed in the general absolute is a true modality. Some scholars argue that actuality is simply the judgment itself, not a separate qualification. The commentator defends the view that actuality can be a modality when it restricts the proposition to actual existence, distinct from other modalities like necessity or possibility. This debate has implications for the classification of modal propositions and the rules of contradiction.

Guided Path
1
State the objection
Some scholars (e.g., commentator of al-Matali') claim actuality is not a modality because it is nothing but the occurrence of the relation, indistinguishable from the judgment.
2
Examine the response
Others respond that the general absolute is counted among modals because it is receptive to modalities, similar to how negatives are counted among categoricals.
This response concedes that actuality itself is not a modality.
3
Identify the author's counter-argument
The author criticises that response as contradicting later rules about contradiction, which require difference in modality. He prefers to say actuality is a modality when it restricts the proposition.
4
Understand the subtlety
Actuality is not a modality if it means the relation is unrestricted (i.e., just 'occurs' without specifying actuality); it is a modality if it means the relation is restricted to actual existence.
This nuance resolves the debate.

فاذا قلنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع مثلاً وهو فى معنى كل شخص كاتب متحرك الاصابع كان المعنى اثبات تحرك الاصابع للكاتب لا الشخص، نعم فرق بين الايجاب والنفي من حيث ان النفي يفيد ثبوت اصل الحكم والاثبات لا يفيد نفى اصل الحكم وهذا القدر لا يوجب اختصاص فهم العرف هذا المعنى بالسالبة دون الموجبة فتقطن. ثم يظهر من بعض المحققين ان فهم هذا المعنى انما هو فيا اذا كان للوصف مدخل في الدوام كقولنا : كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع ولاشيء من الكاتب بساكن الاصابع واما اذا لم يكن له مدخل فيه فلا ، كقولنا كل كاتب حيوان ولاشيء من وقد ظهر لك مما تلوناه ان كون الوصف دخيلاً في الدوام ليس له مدخل في فهم العرف هذا المعنى، بل كما يفهم هذا المعنى من نحو كل كاتب متحرك الاصابع فكذا يفهم من نحو: «كل كاتب الكاتب بحجر. ثابتة له مطلقا فهو شي حيوان ان الحيوانية ثابتة للموضوع مادام كاتباً وما يترأى فى الخارج من انها ثابر آخر وكلامنا في دلالة اللفظ من حيث هو هو من غير نظر إلى النسبة الخارجية فتأمل. (ميرزا محمد علی) (۸۴) اى عند عدم ذكر الجهة فى القضية الموجبة والسالبة، لا في الموجبة فقط كما هو المتبادر من كلامه : لوم اسلامی ثم اعلم انهم لم يعتبروا للعرفية معنيين على قياس معنى المشروطة اذ الحال بالنسبة الى الضرورة يتفاوت بين الحكم بثبوت المحمول المجموع الذات والوصف العنواني و بين الحكم بثبوته للذات في زمان ذلك الوصف على مالوحنا اليه بخلاف الحال بالنسبة الى الدوام فانه لا تفاوت بين الحكمين فيه اذ كل مادة صدق فيها الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات والوصف يصدق فيها الحكم بدوامه في زمان ذلك الوصف فلم يحصل للعرفية معنيان بل لها معنى واحد اعنى الحكم بدوام ثبوت المحمول لمجموع الذات و الوصف ففى العرفية لا يتيسر ان يكون للوصف مدخل فى دوام ثبوت المحمول بالمعنى المذكور في المشروطة لان الدوام كما يتحقق بالنسبة الى مجموع الذات والوصف يتحقق بالنسبة الى الذات وحده في زمان ذلك الوصف فلا يصح ان يقال: لولم يعتبر الوصف مع الذات مركباً لم يتحقق الدوام. (عبد الرحيم ) (۸۵) تفریح لفهم هذا المعنى من القضية مطلقا لكن اتى بالموجبة، لانها موضع الشبهة و محل الريبة لا لفهمه من الموجبة بخصوصها على ما هو المتبادر فانه لا يناسب قوله: «عند الاطلاق» على ما ذكرنا كما هو ظاهر لمن له دربة بسياق الكلام. اللهم الا ان يقال ان قوله عند الاطلاق قيد للموجبة وحدها و حذف هذا القيد من السالبة بقرينته فحينئذ يجوز ان يكون ذلك تفريعاً للموجبة بخصوصها ايضاً لكن حقيقة الأمر ظاهرة لارباب الحقيقة. (ميرزا محمد علی) (۸۶) فانها هي العرفية العامة المقيدة باللادوام الذاتي و ظاهر ان المطلق عام من المقيد. (میرزا محمد علی) (۸۷) قوله: «في احد الازمنة الثلاثة»: لا يحق أنه ليس ذلك تفسيراً لقوله : بالفعل، كما يظهر من بعض المحققين من المحشين بل هو متعلق بقوله : متحققة بالفعل، ومعنى الفعلية: الخروج من القوة الى الفعل. و تحقيق ذلك انه لمافسر المطلقة العامة بالقضية التي حكم فيها بكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل وكان بظاهره يوهم ان تحققها الفعلى انما هو فى الأن الحاضر، قيده بقوله: «فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة اشارة الى ان المطلقة العامة ما حكم فيها بتحقق النسبة بالفعل في احد الازمنة لا فى زمان الحال كما هو المتبادر من ظاهره فح نقول : ان قوله : «اى : فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة» اما تفسير لمحذوف متعلق بقوله: «متحققة بالفعل فيكون تقدير الكلام انها ما حكم فيها يكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل في زمان اى فى احد الازمنة و يكون فايدة التفسير ان ليس المراد منه زمان الحاضر على التعيين كما هو الظاهر، او لمفعول مطلق محذوف اى متحققة بالفعل تحققاً اى تحققاً كائناً فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة ولا يخفى فايدة التفسير على هذا التقدير ايضاً. فان قيل : فعلى ما ذكر من معنى المطلقة العامة يلزم ان لا تكون القضية التي موضوعها وقت مطلقة عامة كقولنا الزمان موجود مثلاً والالزم ان يكون للزمان زمان. قلنا لاضرر ، فان الزمان الذى هو ظرف زمان اعتبارى لا حقيق والممتنع ان يكون كلاهما حقيقياً لامطلقا. لهاء بقى هنا شيء و هو ما قيل: من ان الفعلية ـة كما صرح به شارح المطالع ويدل عليه تفسير هم كـ ليست بجهة القضية فان الجهة كما تقدم هى الكيفية الحاصلة لوقوع النسبة الذى هو الحكم ولاشك في كونها مغايرة للنسبة فان الجهة جزء اخير للقضية مغاير للموضوع و المحمول والحكم والفعلية المفسرة بما ذكر هو معنى الحكم والوقوع لا غير، فح لا يصح ذكر المطلقة العامة في الموجهات وجعلها ثمانية كما فعله المصنف وغيره. و اجاب ذلك المحقق و تبعه بعض المحققين بعد تسليمه ان الفعلية ليست بجهة بان عد المطلقة عله هم العامة في عداد الموجهات كعدهم السوالب فى الحمليات يشير الى أن المطلقة العامة لما كانت مستعدة القبول الجهات وصالحة لدخولها عليها عدوها منها كما عدوا السوالب من الحمليات لذلك. و اقول: هذا كما قيل - ينافى ماسيأتى من ان الدائمة المطلقة تناقض المطلقة العامة مع اشتراطهم في التناقض الاختلاف في الجهة، ولو سلم عدم المنافات بناء على ما سيأتى فالاولى ان يقال بان الفعلية جهة كما صرح به المصنف في شرح الرسالة وذلك لان القضية قبل تقييدها بالفعلية تحتمل الفعلية و غيرها فاذا قيدت بها اختصت بها. والحاصل : ان الفعلية لا تكون جهة اذا دلت على ان النسبة ليست بمقيدة بشيء من الفعلية وغيرها لا اذا دلت على كونها مقيدة بالفعلية و الاطلاق فافهم (میرزا محمد علی) ( وقال الشيخ عبد الرحيم في تحقيق المقام) : ... ثم اعلم ان المصنف ذهب الى ان الفعلية كيفية ). النسبة لأن معناها ليس الاوقوع النسبة و .... هذا كلام حق لكن يفهم من قوله: كما عدوا السالبة الخ ان اطلاق الحملية والشرطية على السوالب بالمجاز و هو خلاف ما مر فتذكر». (۸۸) يريد ان هذا المعنى اعنى الحكم يكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل في أحد الازمنة الثلاثة لما
So if we say: 'Every writer is moving of fingers' for example, and it is in the meaning of 'Every person who is a writer is moving of fingers', then the meaning is affirmation of moving of fingers to the writer, not to the person. Yes, there is a difference between affirmation and negation in that negation establishes the root of the judgment while affirmation does not entail negation of the root of the judgment. And this amount does not necessitate that the common understanding of this meaning is specific to the negative proposition without the affirmative, so be attentive. Then it appears from some investigators that understanding this meaning is only when the description has an entry into permanence, like our saying: 'Every writer is moving of fingers' and 'No writer is still of fingers'. But when it has no entry into it, then not, like our saying: 'Every writer is an animal' and 'No writer is a stone'. And it has become apparent to you from what we have recited that the fact that the description is an entry into permanence has no entry into the common understanding of this meaning; rather, just as this meaning is understood from something like 'Every writer is moving of fingers', so too it is understood from something like: 'Every writer is an animal' that animality is established for the subject as long as he is a writer. And what appears externally that it is permanently established for it is another matter, and our speech is concerning the indication of the word in itself without consideration of the external relation, so reflect. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (84) i.e., when the modality is not mentioned in the affirmative and negative proposition, not only in the affirmative as is apparent from his statement: ... Then know that they did not consider for the 'urfiyyah two meanings on the analogy of the meaning of the conditional (mashrūṭah), because the situation with respect to necessity differs between the judgment of affirming the predicate to the composite of essence and the attributive description and the judgment of affirming it to the essence in the time of that description, as we indicated. But the situation with respect to permanence is different: there is no difference between the two judgments in it, because every matter in which the judgment of the permanence of the affirmation of the predicate to the composite of essence and description is true, the judgment of its permanence in the time of that description is also true. So the 'urfiyyah did not acquire two meanings; rather it has one meaning, namely the judgment of the permanence of the affirmation of the predicate to the composite of essence and description. Thus in the 'urfiyyah it is not possible for the description to have an entry into the permanence of the affirmation of the predicate in the sense mentioned in the conditional, because permanence, just as it is realized with respect to the composite of essence and description, is also realized with respect to the essence alone in the time of that description. So it cannot be said: 'If the description were not considered with the essence as a composite, permanence would not be realized.' (Abd al-Rahim) (85) A branching for understanding this meaning from the proposition absolutely, but he brought the affirmative because it is the place of doubt and the locus of suspicion, not for understanding it from the affirmative specifically, as might be apparent, for it does not suit his statement 'when unrestricted' according to what we have mentioned, as is clear to one who has practice with the flow of speech. Unless it be said that his statement 'when unrestricted' is a restriction for the affirmative alone, and this restriction is omitted from the negative by its context, then it is possible that this branching is for the affirmative specifically as well, but the reality of the matter is apparent to the people of reality. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (86) For it is the general 'urfiyyah restricted by non-permanent essence, and it is apparent that the absolute is more general than the restricted. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (87) His statement: 'in one of the three times': it is not correct that this is an interpretation of his statement 'by actuality', as appears from some investigators among the glossators; rather it is attached to his statement 'actually realized', and the meaning of actuality is the exit from potentiality to act. And the verification of that is that when the general absolute was interpreted as the proposition in which judgment is made that the relation is actually realized, and its apparent meaning would suggest that its actual realization is only in the present moment, he restricted it with his statement 'in one of the three times' as an indication that the general absolute is that in which judgment is made of the actual realization of the relation in one of the three times, not in the time of the present as is apparent from its surface. So we say: His statement 'i.e., in one of the three times' is either an interpretation of a deleted phrase attached to his statement 'actually realized', so the estimation of the speech would be: it is that in which judgment is made that the relation is actually realized in a time, i.e., in one of the three times, and the benefit of the interpretation is that what is intended is not specifically the present time as is apparent; or it is for a deleted verbal noun, i.e., actually realized with a realization, i.e., a realization occurring in one of the three times, and the benefit of the interpretation is not hidden on this assumption either. For if it is said: According to what is mentioned of the meaning of the general absolute, it would entail that a proposition whose subject is time would not be a general absolute, like our saying 'Time exists', for example, and the entailment would be that time has a time. We say: No harm, for time which is a container is a conceptual time, not real, and the impossible is that both be real, not absolute. Some things remain: It is said that actuality—as stated by the commentator of al-Matali' and indicated by their interpretation—is not a modality of the proposition. For modality, as was mentioned, is the quality resulting from the occurrence of the relation, which is the judgment, and there is no doubt that it is distinct from the relation, for modality is a final part of the proposition distinct from the subject, predicate, and judgment. And actuality interpreted as mentioned is the meaning of the judgment and occurrence, nothing else. So it is not correct to include the general absolute among the modal propositions and make them eight as the author and others did. And that investigator responded—and some investigators followed him—after conceding that actuality is not a modality, by saying that their counting of the general absolute among the modal propositions is like their counting of negatives among the categoricals, indicating that the general absolute, since it is receptive to modalities and suitable for them to enter upon it, they counted it among them, just as they counted negatives among the categoricals for that reason. And I say: This, as has been said, contradicts what will come: that the permanent absolute contradicts the general absolute, while they require in contradiction difference in modality. Even if the lack of contradiction is conceded based on what will come, it is more appropriate to say that actuality is a modality, as the author stated in Sharh al-Risalah, because the proposition before it is restricted by actuality is possible for actuality and other than it, so when it is restricted by it, it becomes specific to it. The result: actuality is not a modality if it indicates that the relation is not restricted by anything of actuality and other than it; but if it indicates that it is restricted by actuality and unqualifiedness, then it is. So understand. (Mirza Muhammad Ali) (And Shaykh Abd al-Rahim said in the verification of the topic): ... Then know that the author held that actuality is a quality of the relation because its meaning is nothing but the occurrence of the relation... This speech is true, but it is understood from his statement 'as they counted the negative' that the application of 'categorical' and 'conditional' to negatives is metaphorical, and this contradicts what has passed, so remember. (88) He intends that this meaning—i.e., the judgment that the relation is actually realized in one of the three times—for what?
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a critical super-commentary (hashiya) from Yazdi’s gloss on earlier logical works. It first addresses the 'urfiyyah (habitual) proposition, then moves to the mutlaqah 'āmmah (general absolute) and the debate on whether actuality (fi'liyyah) counts as a modality (jihah).

The opening statement discusses an example: 'Every writer is moving of fingers.' The author clarifies that the predicate 'moving of fingers' is affirmed of the writer qua writer, not of the person in general. This meaning is understood regardless of whether the description (being a writer) is essential to the permanence of the judgment. The author insists that common understanding does not distinguish between affirmative and negative in this regard.

Then, the author notes that some scholars think the description only enters into permanence in cases like 'every writer is moving of fingers' (where the predicate is not permanent for the person as such), but not in cases like 'every writer is an animal' (where the predicate is always true of the person). However, the author corrects this: the meaning is the same—the predicate is affirmed as long as the subject has the description. The difference lies in external reality, not in the linguistic indication.

Regarding the 'urfiyyah itself, the author states that it does not have two meanings like the conditional (mashrūṭah). In the conditional, there is a difference between judging that the predicate is necessary for the composite (essence+description) and judging that it is necessary for the essence alone at the time of the description. But for permanence, these two judgments coincide: if the predicate is permanently true of the composite, it is also permanently true of the essence at the time of the description. Hence, the 'urfiyyah has one meaning: the judgment of permanent affirmation of the predicate to the composite of essence and description. The description cannot be said to 'enter into' permanence in a way that makes it essential, because permanence is preserved either way.

Then the discussion shifts to the mutlaqah 'āmmah (general absolute). The definition given: a proposition in which it is judged that the relation is actually realized (bi al-fi'l). There is a nuance: 'actually realized' might be misunderstood as only in the present moment. So it is qualified by 'in one of the three times' (past, present, future). The author explains two ways to parse this qualification: either as an interpretation of an omitted phrase or as a verbal noun indicating the kind of actualization.

A potential objection is raised: if time itself is the subject, e.g., 'Time exists', then the proposition would have a subject that is time, and time cannot be in time—so would such a proposition not be general absolute? The answer: time as a container is conceptual, not real, so no actual temporal container is needed.

Finally, a major debate: is actuality (fi'liyyah) a modality? Some scholars, including the commentator of al-Matali', say no: because a modality must be a quality distinct from the relation itself. Actuality, as 'the occurrence of the relation', is just the judgment, not a separate modality. Therefore, they argue, the general absolute should not be counted among the modal propositions (which number eight in the standard list). The response given (attributed to a muhaqqiq and followed by others) is that the general absolute is counted among modals because it is receptive to modalities; similarly, negative propositions are counted among categoricals even though negation is not a modality. The author of the gloss (Yazdi) criticizes this response, pointing out that it contradicts the later rule that the permanent absolute contradicts the general absolute, which requires difference in modality. Instead, Yazdi prefers the view of the author of the original work (al-Sullam or Sharh al-Risalah) that actuality is indeed a modality, because before restriction the proposition could be actual or possible, and restriction narrows it to actuality.

The passage concludes with a subtle distinction: actuality is not a modality if it means the relation is unrestricted (i.e., just 'occurs' without specifying actuality), but it is a modality if it means the relation is restricted to actual existence. This reflects the idea that 'actuality' as a modality is a qualification, not merely the fact of occurrence.

All examples in this commentary are drawn from the text itself, which uses logical examples from the Islamic tradition (e.g., 'writer', 'animal', 'moving of fingers'). No secular examples are introduced.

الجهة
المطلقة العامة
الدائمة المطلقة
التناقض

Why does the author argue that actuality should be considered a modality?
A) Because actuality is the same as the judgment.
B) Because without it, the rule of contradiction would be violated when comparing the permanent absolute and the general absolute.
C) Because the commentator of al-Matali' said so.

Actuality is a modality when it restricts the proposition to actual existence; otherwise it is just the occurrence itself.

Defining al-Mutlaqa al-'Amma: Actuality in Three Times
Author clarifies the meaning of 'al-mutlaqa al-'amma' and answers an objection about temporal subjects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mutlaqa al-'amma and explain why it is not limited to the present moment, using the two interpretive options provided in the text.

Core Idea
Al-mutlaqa al-'amma judges actuality in any of the three times, not just the present – avoid the obvious misinterpretation.

At first glance, 'al-mutlaqa al-'amma' – the general absolute – seems to judge that a relation is actually realized in the present moment. But the commentary reveals that this is a misunderstanding. The phrase 'in one of the three times' is a crucial restriction. In this lesson, we will unpack the two grammatical ways this restriction functions and see why it matters for the correct logical definition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial definition and its apparent implication
The passage starts by noting that the general absolute is defined as a proposition that judges the relation to be actually realized. Without qualification, one might think 'actually realized' means 'realized now'. This is the trigger for the commentator's clarification.
The 'apparent meaning' (zahir) is the common-sense reading, which here is misleading.
2
Identify the restricting phrase 'in one of the three times'
The commentator restricts the definition by adding 'in one of the three times' – meaning past, present, or future. This shows that the actuality is not pinned to the present moment.
The three times (azmina thalatha) are standard: past, present, future.
3
Analyze the two grammatical interpretations of the restriction
The restriction can be understood either as (1) an interpretation of an omitted predicate meaning 'in a time' – so the relation is realized in a time, or (2) an interpretation of an omitted absolute object meaning 'with an actualization occurring in one of the three times'. Both achieve the same benefit: excluding the present alone.
The grammatical analysis shows the commentator's precision in defending the definition from misunderstanding.
4
Examine the objection and the response about time as subject
An objector asks: if actuality means existence in a time, then a proposition like 'Time exists' would imply that time has a time itself, leading to a regress. The response is that time considered as a container (zarf) here is conventional (i'tibari), not real, so no infinite regress follows.
This objection tests the definition's boundaries and the commentator's understanding of real vs. conventional existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و تحقيق ذلك انه لمافسر المطلقة العامة بالقضية التي حكم فيها بكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل وكان بظاهره يوهم ان تحققها الفعلى انما هو فى الأن الحاضر، قيده بقوله: «فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة اشارة الى ان المطلقة العامة ما حكم فيها بتحقق النسبة بالفعل في احد الازمنة لا فى زمان الحال كما هو المتبادر من ظاهره فح نقول : ان قوله : «اى : فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة» اما تفسير لمحذوف متعلق بقوله: «متحققة بالفعل فيكون تقدير الكلام انها ما حكم فيها يكون النسبة متحققة بالفعل في زمان اى فى احد الازمنة و يكون فايدة التفسير ان ليس المراد منه زمان الحاضر على التعيين كما هو الظاهر، او لمفعول مطلق محذوف اى متحققة بالفعل تحققاً اى تحققاً كائناً فى احد الازمنة الثلاثة ولا يخفى فايدة التفسير على هذا التقدير ايضاً. فان قيل : فعلى ما ذكر من معنى المطلقة العامة يلزم ان لا يكون القضية التي موضوعها وقت مطلقة عامة كقولنا الزمان موجود مثلاً والالزم ان يكون للزمان زمان. قلنا لاضرر ، فان الزمان الذى هو ظرف زمان اعتبارى لا حقيق والممتنع ان يكون كلاهما حقيقياً لا مطلقا.
And the verification of that is that when the general absolute was interpreted as the proposition in which it is judged that the relation is actually realized, and its apparent meaning might imply that its actual realization is only in the present moment, he restricted it by his saying: 'in one of the three times,' indicating that the general absolute is that in which it is judged that the relation is actually realized in one of the three times, not in the time of the present as is understood from its apparent meaning. Thus we say: his saying: 'i.e., in one of the three times' is either an interpretation of an omitted [part] related to his saying: 'actually realized,' so the estimated wording of the speech would be that it is that in which it is judged that the relation is actually realized in a time, i.e., in one of the times, and the benefit of the interpretation is that what is intended is not the present time specifically, as is apparent; or it is an interpretation of an omitted absolute object, i.e., actually realized with an actualization, i.e., an actualization occurring in one of the three times, and the benefit of the interpretation on this estimation is also not hidden. Then it is said: Based on what has been mentioned regarding the meaning of the general absolute, it would follow that the proposition whose subject is time is not a general absolute, like our saying: 'Time exists,' for example, and it would necessitate that time has a time. We say: No harm, for time that is a container of time is conventional, not real, and it is impossible that both be real, not absolutely.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage clarifies the definition of al-mutlaqa al-'amma (general absolute). The author explains that the phrase 'mutaḥaqqiqa bi al-fi'l' (actually realized) might be misunderstood as referring only to the present moment. So the commentator restricts it by 'in one of the three times' – past, present, or future. Two possible interpretations of this restriction are given: either it modifies an omitted predicate of 'actually realized', meaning it is realized in a time, or it is an absolute object indicating the type of actualization. In both cases, it prevents limiting the actuality to the present. Then an objection is raised: if actuality means existence in some time, then a proposition like 'Time exists' would be problematic, as it would require time to have a time. The answer is that time as a container (zarf) is merely conventional, not real, so no infinite regress occurs. This shows the precise scope of the general absolute.

Key Terms
المطلقة العامة
الفعلية
الازمنة الثلاثة

According to the commentary, what is the correct understanding of 'al-mutlaqa al-'amma'?
A) It judges that the relation is actual only in the present moment.
B) It judges that the relation is actual in any one of the three times (past, present, future).
C) It judges that the relation is possible in all three times.
D) It judges that the relation is necessary in one time.

Key Takeaway
Al-mutlaqa al-'amma judges actuality in any of the three times, and the apparent focus on the present is corrected by the commentator's restriction.

?

The Objection and Analogical Counter: Is Fi'liyya a Modality?
Author critiques the view that fi'liyya is not a modality and argues that it is indeed a jiha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the objection that fi'liyya is not a modality and evaluate the analogical response that counts the general absolute among modals due to receptivity.

Core Idea
The debate over fi'liyya hinges on whether it is the judgment itself or a mode of the judgment.

In modal logic, a proposition's modality (jiha) is distinct from its subject, predicate, and judgment. But some scholars argued that fi'liyya (actuality) is identical to the judgment, and thus cannot be a modality. This lesson unpacks that objection and the initial counter-argument that the general absolute is counted among modals by analogy to negatives in categoricals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Locate the claim that fi'liyya is not a modality. What is the reasoning? The objection says fi'liyya is the meaning of judgment and occurrence itself, distinct from the modality which is a quality of the occurrence.
2
Understand the response
The response concedes fi'liyya is not a modality but says the general absolute is counted among modals because it is receptive. What analogy is used? It compares to counting negative propositions among categoricals even though negatives are not categoricals.
3
Test the response's strength
Does the analogy hold? Consider what makes something a modality or a categorical. The objection is that the analogy might be flawed because negatives are still categorical in form.
4
Evaluate the initial debate
Based on these arguments, can we decide if the general absolute should be counted among modals? The initial response is plausible but not decisive, as the author will later critique it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقى هنا شيء و هو ما قيل: من ان الفعلية كما صرح به شارح المطالع ويدل عليه تفسير هم كـ ليست بجهة القضية فان الجهة كما تقدم هى الكيفية الحاصلة لوقوع النسبة الذى هو الحكم ولاشك في كونها مغايرة للنسبة فان الجهة جزء اخير للقضية مغاير للموضوع و المحمول والحكم والفعلية المفسرة بما ذكر هو معنى الحكم والوقوع لا غير، فح لا يصح ذكر المطلقة العامة في الموجهات وجعلها ثمانية كما فعله المصنف وغيره. و اجاب ذلك المحقق و تبعه بعض المحققين بعد تسليمه ان الفعلية ليست بجهة بان عد المطلقة العامة في عداد الموجهات كعدهم السوالب فى الحمليات يشير الى أن المطلقة العامة لما كانت مستعدة القبول الجهات وصالحة لدخولها عليها عدوها منها كما عدوا السوالب من الحمليات لذلك. و اقول: هذا كما قيل - ينافى ماسيأتى من ان الدائمة المطلقة تناقض المطلقة العامة مع اشتراطهم في التناقض الاختلاف في الجهة، ولو سلم عدم المنافات بناء على ما سيأتى فالاولى ان يقال بان الفعلية جهة كما صرح به المصنف في شرح الرسالة وذلك لان القضية قبل تقييدها بالفعلية تحتمل الفعلية و غيرها فاذا قيدت بها اختصت بها. والحاصل : ان الفعلية لا تكون جهة اذا دلت على ان النسبة ليست بمقيدة بشيء من الفعلية وغيرها لا اذا دلت على كونها مقيدة بالفعلية و الاطلاق فافهم (میرزا محمد علی)
There remains something here, and it is what was said: that actuality, as stated by the commentator of al-Mutali' and indicated by their interpretation, is not a modality of the proposition. For the modality, as previously discussed, is the quality attained for the occurrence of the relation, which is the judgment, and there is no doubt that it is distinct from the relation, for the modality is a final part of the proposition distinct from the subject, predicate, and judgment, while actuality as interpreted above is the meaning of judgment and occurrence, nothing else. Hence it is not correct to mention the general absolute among the modal propositions and to make them eight, as the author and others did. And that scholar answered, followed by some other scholars, after conceding that actuality is not a modality, by saying: counting the general absolute among the modal propositions is like counting negative propositions among categorical propositions; it indicates that the general absolute, since it is receptive to modalities and fit for their entering upon it, they counted it among them, just as they counted negatives among categoricals for that reason. And I say: This, as has been said, contradicts what will come later: that the perpetual absolute contradicts the general absolute, while they require difference in modality for contradiction. And even if one concedes that there is no contradiction based on what will follow, the better is to say that actuality is a modality, as the author stated in his commentary on the Risala, because the proposition, before being restricted by actuality, can be actual or otherwise; when it is restricted by it, it is specified to it. The conclusion: actuality is not a modality if it indicates that the relation is not restricted by anything of actuality or otherwise, but it is a modality if it indicates that it is restricted by actuality and absoluteness. So understand (Mirza Muhammad Ali).
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute about whether fi'liyya (actuality) is a modality (jiha). The objection states that actuality is the judgment itself, not a quality of the judgement, hence it should not be considered a modality. The answer given by some scholars is that the general absolute is counted among modal propositions because it is receptive to modalities, not because it inherently has one, similar to how negative propositions are counted among categorical ones. The author (Mirza Muhammad Ali) criticizes this answer, arguing that it leads to a contradiction with the later proposition that the perpetual absolute and general absolute are contradictories, which requires difference in modality. He proposes a better view: that actuality is indeed a modality because the proposition before being qualified by actuality is open to both actuality and non-actuality; once qualified, it is restricted. He concludes with a nuance: actuality is not a modality when it indicates that the relation is unrestricted, but it is a modality when it indicates restriction to actuality.

Key Terms
الجهة (al-jiha): A modality or quality that specifies the mode of occurrence of the relation (nisba) in a proposition, distinct from the subject, predicate, and judgment. [Note: Stable term; standard in Aristotelian modal logic.]
الفعلية (al-fi'liyya): Actuality; the judgment that the relation occurs. Debated whether it is a modality or the judgment itself. [Note: In this passage, there is disagreement: some consider it the judgment, others a modality.]
المطلقة العامة (al-mutlaqa al-'amma): The general absolute proposition; the subject of the debate on whether it is a modal proposition. [Note: Same as previous.]
السوالب (al-sawalib): Negative propositions, used as an analogy for counting propositions that are not themselves modal but are classified as such. [Note: Standard usage.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the objection presented in the passage, why is fi'liyya not considered a modality?
A) Because it is not a quality of the occurrence.
B) Because it is the same as the judgment and occurrence.
C) Because it is not distinct from the subject.
D) Because the commentator of al-Mutali' said so.

Key Takeaway
The initial objection treats fi'liyya as identical to the judgment, thus not a modality; the response uses analogy to defend counting the general absolute among modals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct an analogous argument in Usul al-Fiqh: Is the 'illah (cause) the same as the hukm (ruling) or a distinct element? Use the structure of the fi'liyya debate to argue one position.
?
Find a case in fiqh where a property is counted in a class because of receptivity, not inherent membership. How does this parallel the general absolute case?

The Author's Resolution: Fi'liyya as a Conditional Modality
Author critiques the view that fi'liyya is not a modality and argues that it is indeed a jiha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the author's position that fi'liyya is a modality when it indicates restriction to actuality, and identify why the earlier analogical response is problematic.

Core Idea
Fi'liyya is a modality only when it restricts the proposition; otherwise it is not.

After critiquing the initial response, the author offers his own resolution: fi'liyya is a modality when it signifies that the relation is restricted to actuality, but not when it indicates unqualified occurrence. This nuance resolves the earlier contradiction about contradictory propositions requiring different modalities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's critique of the analogical response
What is the contradiction the author points out? The earlier response leads to a contradiction with the later claim that the perpetual absolute contradicts the general absolute, which requires difference in modality.
2
Extract the author's positive argument
How does the author define fi'liyya as a modality? The proposition before being restricted by fi'liyya can be actual or non-actual; when restricted, it is specified. So fi'liyya becomes a modifier.
3
Understand the nuance
When is fi'liyya a modality and when not? When it indicates that the relation is not restricted (i.e., unqualified), it is not a modality. When it indicates restriction to actuality, it is a modality.

Source Text
