The General Possible Proposition: Does It Contain a Judgment?
Author examines whether al-mumkina al-'amma contains a judgment and can be considered a modal proposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the debate over whether al-mumkina al-'amma contains a judgment and justify its classification as a potential rather than actual modal proposition.

Core Idea
The general possible proposition contains no actual judgment but is a proposition potentially, similar to mixed propositions.

Is a statement like 'Zayd may write' a genuine proposition? The logicians debate whether al-mumkina al-'amma (general possible) contains a judgment in the affirmative side. This lesson unpacks the dilemma and its resolution, showing how possibility is defined and why this matters for classifying propositions in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dilemma
The author presents two alternatives: if the general possible contains a judgment in the affirmative side, it would have two judgments (the relation and its possibility) and cannot be simple; if it contains no judgment, it is not a proposition at all. Pinpoint this logical fork.
2
Examine the proposed solution
One might define possibility as negation of impossibility from the affirmative side, which seems to add a judgment. But the author responds that this only negates impossibility, not a positive judgment. Grasp the difference between 'not impossible' and 'possible as a positive fact'.
3
Understand the equivalence of two definitions
The verification: negation of necessity from the opposite side is equivalent to negation of impossibility from the affirmative side. If you negate one, the other follows. This means both definitions convey the same meaning.
4
Recognize the resolution via potentiality
Some scholars resolve the dilemma by considering the possible proposition as a proposition potentially (bil-quwwa), not actually. They count it among modals because it is receptive to modality. Note how this parallels the treatment of mixed propositions.
5
Apply the analogy to the general absolute
The author argues that once potentiality is accepted, the possible proposition actually has a modality because the negation of necessity is a quality of the relation, analogous to how the general absolute (al-mutlaqa al-'amma) is considered modal. See the logic of this extension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد ظهر من ذلك ان الممكنة العامة غير مشتملة على الحكم في الجانب الموافق كما صرح به بعضهم فح لا يصح عدها قضية فضلاً عن كونها بسيطة أو موجهة وبالجملة ان قيل بأن الممكنة العامة مشتملة على الحكم في الجانب الموافق لم يصح عدها من البسايط لاشتمالهاح على حكمين مختلفين وان قيل بانها غير مشتملة عليه، لم يصح عدها قضية اعم من كونها بسيطة أو موجهة. :لا يقال انا نختار الشق الأول ونقول : ان معنى الامكان سلب الامتناع عن الطرف الموافق كما فسره بذلك قوم، فح يصح عدها من البسائط لاشتمالهاح على الحكم في الجانب الموافق دون المخالف ولا يرد شيء لانانقول: لانسلم ان الامكان بذلك المعنى يدل على الحكم في الجانب الموافق، غاية الامرانه يدل على ان تلك النسبة المذكورة غير ممتعة و ليس هذا حكماً بوقوعها مع ان التحقيق: ان الامكان بهذا المعنى عين الامكان بذلك المعنى في المعنى فان سلب الضرورة عن الجانب المخالف يلزمه سلب الامتناع عن الطرف الموافق وبالعكس. قال بعض المحققين ان الممكنة وان لم يكن فيها فى الطرف الموافق حكم اصلاً حتى يحتمل ان يكون واقعاً و ان لا يكون، بل انما حكم فيها بسلب الضرورة عن الطرف المتخالف فقط، فالمطلقة العامة هي القضية بالفعل والموجهة بالقوة والممكنة ليست قضية الا بالقوة فضلاً عن كونها موجهة بالفعل لكن لما كان مرادهم بالقضية اعم من ان تكون بالفعل أو بالقوة وقد صرحوا بان الموضوع و المحمول والنسبة بينهما قضية، الا ترى انهم عدوا المختطلات فى القضايا ولا حكم فيها بالفعل صح عدهم اياها في عداد القضايا بل عدهم اياها من الموجهات ايضاً انها بملاحظة صلاحيتها للجهة بالقوة وان لم تكن لهاجهة بالفعل كما عدوا المطلقة العامة منها بهذه الملاحظة أيضاً. و اقول : اذا ثبت كونها قضية بهذه الملاحظة أو لغيرها مما قيل امكن لنا ان نقول باشتمالها على الجهة بالفعل، ضرورة ان سلب الضرورة عن الطرف المخالف كيفية حاصلة للنسبة فانها قبل تقييدها بالامكان كانت محتملة لذلك و غيره حتى يمكن ان يكون طرفها المخالف ضرورياً واذا قيدت به علم ان ذلك الطرف ليس بضرورى ولاشك في كونها كيفية مخالفة لاصل الحكم وهذا نظير ما قلنا في المطلقة العامة، فافهم وتأمل (میرزا محمد علی) :(۹۱) قوله :(یعنی: ان الكتابة غير مستحيلة له أعلم ان للامكان تفسيرين احدهما سلب الضرورة الذاتية عن الجانب المخالف للحكم وثانيهما سلب الامتناع الذاتي عن الجانب الموافق
Thus it has become clear from that that the general possible does not contain a judgment in the affirmative side, as some have stated, so it is not correct to count it as a proposition, let alone as a simple or modal. In summary: if it is said that the general possible contains a judgment in the affirmative side, it is not correct to count it among the simple propositions because it would contain two different judgments; and if it is said that it does not contain it, it is not correct to count it as a proposition at all, whether simple or modal. You cannot say: we choose the first alternative and say that the meaning of possibility is the negation of impossibility from the affirmative side, as some have interpreted it, for then it would be correct to count it among the simple propositions because it contains a judgment in the affirmative side without the opposite, and nothing is refuted. For we say: we do not accept that possibility in that meaning indicates a judgment in the affirmative side; at most it indicates that that mentioned relation is not impossible, and this is not a judgment of its occurrence, while the verification is that possibility in this meaning is identical in meaning to possibility in that meaning, for the negation of necessity from the opposite side entails the negation of impossibility from the affirmative side, and vice versa. Some scholars said: although the possible does not have any judgment in the affirmative side at all, so that it could be actual or not, rather it only judges the negation of necessity from the opposite side, so the general absolute is an actual proposition and the modal is potential, and the possible is only a proposition potentially, let alone being an actual modal; but since their intention by 'proposition' is broader than actual or potential, and they have stated that the subject, predicate, and the relation between them constitute a proposition, do you not see that they counted mixed propositions among propositions even though there is no actual judgment in them? Thus it is correct to count them among propositions, and they even count them among modals as well, because they consider their receptivity to modality potentially, even if they do not have a modality actually, just as they counted the general absolute among them on this consideration. And I say: If it is established that it is a proposition on this consideration or other than what was said, it is possible for us to say that it includes the modality actually, necessarily, for the negation of necessity from the opposite side is a quality attained for the relation, for before it was restricted by possibility, it was possible to be otherwise, even for the opposite side to be necessary, and when it is restricted by it, it is known that that side is not necessary, and there is no doubt that it is a quality distinct from the original judgment, and this is analogous to what we said regarding the general absolute. So understand and reflect (Mirza Muhammad Ali). His saying: (meaning: writing is not impossible for him) Know that possibility has two interpretations: one is the negation of essential necessity from the side opposite to the judgment, and the second is the negation of essential impossibility from the affirmative side.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage discusses the status of al-mumkina al-'amma (the general possible proposition). The author first presents a dilemma: if the possible proposition is interpreted as containing a judgment in the affirmative side (i.e., the relation is possible), then it would contain two judgments (the possibility and the relation itself), so it cannot be simple; if it does not contain a judgment in the affirmative side, then it is not a proposition at all. One might object by choosing the first interpretation and defining possibility as negation of impossibility from the affirmative side, which would make it simple. But the response is that this definition still does not yield a positive judgment of occurrence; it only negates impossibility. The verification is that the two interpretations of possibility (negation of necessity from the opposite side and negation of impossibility from the affirmative side) are equivalent. Some scholars resolve this by considering the possible as a proposition potentially, not actually, and they count it among modals because it is receptive to modality. The author (Mirza Muhammad Ali) then argues that once we accept it as a proposition potentially, we can also say it actually has a modality, because the negation of necessity from the opposite side is a quality attained for the relation, similar to the general absolute. The passage concludes with a definition of the two interpretations of possibility.

Key Terms
الممكنة العامة (al-mumkina al-'amma)
الامكان (al-imkan)
الجانب الموافق (al-janib al-muwafiq)
الجانب المخالف (al-janib al-mukhalif)
المطلقة العامة (al-mutlaqa al-'amma)
المختلطات (al-mukhtalatat)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do some scholars count the general possible proposition among modals?
A) Because it contains a positive judgment of possibility.
B) Because it is receptive to modality potentially, like mixed propositions.
C) Because it is equivalent to the general absolute in all respects.
D) Because it negates impossibility from the affirmative side.

Key Takeaway
The general possible proposition is a modal proposition potentially, not actually, but because the negation of necessity is a real quality of the relation, it can be considered to have modality actually, analogously to the general absolute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the proposition 'It is permissible to break the fast while traveling' (from fiqh). Analyze whether it contains a judgment in the affirmative side (affirming permissibility) or only negates prohibition. Use the two definitions of possibility to clarify its logical form.
?
Consider the statement 'Zayd may be knowledgeable.' Is this a modal proposition actually or potentially? Justify your answer using the author's argument about the potential proposition and the quality of the relation.
